        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.1c08632"><meta property="og:title" content="Binary-Metal Mn2SnO4 Nanoparticles and Sn Confined in a Cubic Frame with N-Doped Carbon for Enhanced Lithium and Sodium Storage"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/acsami.1c08632.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Sn-based materials have been popularly researched as anodes for energy storage due to their high theoretical capacity. However, the sluggish reaction kinetics and unsatisfied cycling stability caused by poor conductivity and dramatic volume expansion are still pivotal barriers for the development of Sn-based materials as anodes. In this work, the binary-metal Mn2SnO4 nanoparticles and Sn encapsulated in N-doped carbon (Sn@Mn2SnO4-NC) were fabricated by multistep reactions and employed as the anode for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs). The coexistence of binary metals (Sn and Mn) can improve intrinsic conductivity. Simultaneously, hollow architecture along with carbon relieves internal stress and prevents structural collapse. A Sn@Mn2SnO4-NC anode delivers an appealing capacity of 1039.5 mAh g–1 for 100 cycles at 100 mA g–1 and 823.8 mAh g–1 for 600 cycles at 1000 mA g–1 in LIBs. When evaluated as an anode in SIBs, the Sn@Mn2SnO4-NC anode tolerates up to 7000 cycles at 2000 mA g–1 and maintains a capacity of 185.8 mAh g–1. Quantified kinetic investigations demonstrate the high contribution of pseudocapacitive effects during the cycle process. Furthermore, density functional theory (DFT) calculations further verify that introduction of the second metal (Mn) improves the conductivity of the material, which is favorable for charge transport. This work is expected to provide a feasible preparation strategy for binary-metal materials to enhance the performance of lithium- and sodium-ion batteries."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/acsami.1c08632.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/1122814~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="931880bdca4654b8-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="931880bdca4654b8-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: 'ec10eb5c-afe0-46e1-972f-c124b909cdf9'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

img{border:0}.a2a_button_facebook_like iframe{max-width:none}</style><script charset="utf-8" async="" src="https://script.hotjar.com/modules.f98993dba31a932bc912.js"></script><script id="yui__dyn_0" type="text/javascript" src="https://www2.snapengage.com/chatjs/ServiceGetConfig?w=921a4ec7-cecf-43a6-afa5-6cd1346520b1"></script><script type="osano/blocked" async=""></script><script charset="utf-8" src="https://pubs.acs.org/products/achs/releasedAssets/js/vendors~lazy-imports-c0b82d66d33565b4cebe.js"></script><script charset="utf-8" src="https://pubs.acs.org/products/achs/releasedAssets/js/lazy-imports-6922fe6a4ca6b2e0cd9a.js"></script><script type="text/javascript" src="/specs/products/achs/releasedAssets/public/mathjax-0a9852ad89643b94fe5099b753f6a294/MathJax.js?config=TeX-AMS-MML_HTMLorMML"></script><script type="text/x-mathjax-config;executed=true">MathJax.Hub.Config({
            menuSettings: {
                zoom: "Click",
                zscale: "150%"
            },
            SVG: {
                fonts: ["STIX-Web"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
            },
            "HTML-CSS": {
                fonts: ["STIX"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
                scale: 90,
            },
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("mml Jax Ready", function () {
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            MML.mi.prototype.setTeXclass = function (prev) {
                this.getPrevClass(prev);
                return this;
            };
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                setTeXclass: function (prev) {
                    this.getPrevClass(prev);
                    for (var i = 0, m = this.data.length; i < m; i++) {
                        if (this.data[i]) this.data[i].setTeXclass();
                    }
                    return this;
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("SVG Jax Ready", function () {
            var FONT = MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"] || MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"];
            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("MathML Jax Ready", function () {
            var PARSE = MathJax.InputJax.MathML.Parse;
            var ADD = PARSE.prototype.AddChildren;
            PARSE.Augment({
                AddChildren: function (mml, node) {
                    ADD.call(this, mml, node);
                    if (mml.type === 'mrow') {
                        var first = mml.data[0], last = mml.data[mml.data.length-1];
                        if (mml.open && !mml.data[0].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.open;
                        if (mml.close && !mml.data[mml.data.length - 1].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.close;
                    }
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS Jax Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax['HTML-CSS'];
            var DELIMITERS = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.DELIMITERS;
            var FONT = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"] || HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"]

            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;

            MML.mrow.Augment({
              _HTMLlineBreaks: MML.mrow.prototype.HTMLlineBreaks,
              HTMLlineBreaks: function (span) {

                if (this.parent.linebreakContainer && this.Get("display") === "inline") return false;
                return this._HTMLlineBreaks(span);
              }
            });


            DELIMITERS[0x0305] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x00AF};
            DELIMITERS[0x033F] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x003D};
            DELIMITERS[0x20E1] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x2194};

            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS multiline Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax["HTML-CSS"];
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            var PENALTY = MML.mbase.prototype.HTMLlinebreakPenalty;

            MML.msqrt.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mroot.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mspace.Augment({
                defaultDef: {
                    indentalign: MML.INDENTALIGN.AUTO,
                    indentshift: "0",
                    indenttarget: "",
                    indentalignfirst: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftfirst: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT,
                    indentalignlast: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftlast: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT
                },
                HTMLbetterBreak: function (info,state) {
                    if (info.values && info.values.id === this.spanID) {return false}
                    var values = this.getValues(
                        "linebreak",
                        "indentalign","indentshift",
                        "indentalignfirst","indentshiftfirst",
                        "indentalignlast","indentshiftlast"
                    );
                    var linebreakValue = values.linebreak;
                    if (!linebreakValue || this.hasDimAttr()) {
                        linebreakValue = MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO;
                    }
                    var W = info.scanW, span = this.HTMLspanElement(), w = span.bbox.w;
                    if (span.style.paddingLeft) {w += HTMLCSS.unEm(span.style.paddingLeft)}
                    if (W - info.shift === 0) {return false} // don't break at zero width
                    var offset = HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth - W;

                    if (state.n === 0 && (values.indentshiftfirst !== state.VALUES.indentshiftfirst ||
                        values.indentalignfirst !== state.VALUES.indentalignfirst)) {
                        var align = this.HTMLgetAlign(state,values),
                            shift = this.HTMLgetShift(state,values,align);
                        offset += (info.shift - shift);
                    }

                    var penalty = Math.floor(offset / HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth * 1000);
                    if (penalty < 0) {penalty = PENALTY.toobig - 3*penalty}
                    penalty += info.nest * PENALTY.nestfactor;

                    var linebreak = PENALTY[linebreakValue]||0;
                    if (linebreakValue === MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO && w >= PENALTY.spacelimit &&
                        !this.mathbackground && !this.background)
                    {linebreak = [(w+PENALTY.spaceoffset)*PENALTY.spacefactor]}
                    if (!MathJax.Object.isArray(linebreak)) {
                        if (linebreak || offset >= 0) {penalty = linebreak * info.nest}
                    } else {penalty = Math.max(1,penalty + linebreak[0] * info.nest)}

                    if (penalty >= info.penalty) {return false}
                    info.penalty = penalty; info.values = values; info.W = W; info.w = w;
                    values.lineleading = state.VALUES.lineleading;
                    values.linebreakstyle = "before"; values.id = this.spanID;
                    return true;
                }
            });


            
            PENALTY.goodbreak = [-400];

        });</script><style type="text/css">.MathJax_Hover_Frame {border-radius: .25em; -webkit-border-radius: .25em; -moz-border-radius: .25em; -khtml-border-radius: .25em; box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -webkit-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -moz-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -khtml-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; border: 1px solid #A6D ! important; display: inline-block; position: absolute}

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="931880bdca4654b8-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

href="/action/showCitFormats?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c08632&amp;href=/doi/10.1021/acsami.1c08632" title="Cite This" class="figure-viewer-cite-this-link"><i class="icon-check-circle"></i><span><strong>Cite <script nonce="931880bdca4654b8-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Binary-Metal Mn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;SnO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt; Nanoparticles and Sn Confined in a Cubic Frame with N-Doped Carbon for Enhanced Lithium and Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c08632", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Binary-Metal Mn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;SnO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt; Nanoparticles and Sn Confined in a Cubic Frame with N-Doped Carbon for Enhanced Lithium and Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c08632", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Binary-Metal Mn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;SnO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt; Nanoparticles and Sn Confined in a Cubic Frame with N-Doped Carbon for Enhanced Lithium and Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c08632", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Binary-Metal Mn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;SnO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt; Nanoparticles and Sn Confined in a Cubic Frame with N-Doped Carbon for Enhanced Lithium and Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c08632", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Binary-Metal Mn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;SnO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt; Nanoparticles and Sn Confined in a Cubic Frame with N-Doped Carbon for Enhanced Lithium and Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c08632", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Binary-Metal Mn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;SnO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt; Nanoparticles and Sn Confined in a Cubic Frame with N-Doped Carbon for Enhanced Lithium and Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c08632", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Binary-Metal Mn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;SnO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt; Nanoparticles and Sn Confined in a Cubic Frame with N-Doped Carbon for Enhanced Lithium and Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c08632", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Binary-Metal Mn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;SnO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt; Nanoparticles and Sn Confined in a Cubic Frame with N-Doped Carbon for Enhanced Lithium and Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c08632", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Binary-Metal Mn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;SnO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt; Nanoparticles and Sn Confined in a Cubic Frame with N-Doped Carbon for Enhanced Lithium and Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c08632", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

Find more information on<a href="https://help.altmetric.com/support/solutions/articles/6000233311-how-is-the-altmetric-attention-score-calculated"> the Altmetric Attention Score and how the score is calculated.</a></p></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_0009.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/large/am1c08632_0009.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c08632&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Sn-based materials have been popularly researched as anodes for energy storage due to their high theoretical capacity. However, the sluggish reaction kinetics and unsatisfied cycling stability caused by poor conductivity and dramatic volume expansion are still pivotal barriers for the development of Sn-based materials as anodes. In this work, the binary-metal Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub> nanoparticles and Sn encapsulated in N-doped carbon (Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC) were fabricated by multistep reactions and employed as the anode for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs). The coexistence of binary metals (Sn and Mn) can improve intrinsic conductivity. Simultaneously, hollow architecture along with carbon relieves internal stress and prevents structural collapse. A Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC anode delivers an appealing capacity of 1039.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> for 100 cycles at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup> and 823.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> for 600 cycles at 1000 mA g<sup>–1</sup> in LIBs. When evaluated as an anode in SIBs, the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC anode tolerates up to 7000 cycles at 2000 mA g<sup>–1</sup> and maintains a capacity of 185.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>. Quantified kinetic investigations demonstrate the high contribution of pseudocapacitive effects during the cycle process. Furthermore, density functional theory (DFT) calculations further verify that introduction of the second metal (Mn) improves the conductivity of the material, which is favorable for charge transport. This work is expected to provide a feasible preparation strategy for binary-metal materials to enhance the performance of lithium- and sodium-ion batteries.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D38278%26pageCount%3D11%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DShuyun%2BWan%252C%2BQiming%2BLiu%252C%2BMing%2BCheng%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D13%26issueNum%3D32%26contentID%3Dacsami.1c08632%26title%3DBinary-Metal%2BMn2SnO4%2BNanoparticles%2Band%2BSn%2BConfined%2Bin%2Ba%2BCubic%2BFrame%2Bwith%2BN-Doped%2BCarbon%2Bfor%2BEnhanced%2BLithium%2Band%2BSodium%2BStorage%26numPages%3D11%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D38288%26publicationDate%3DAugust%2B2021" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2021 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">
                                        Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291517&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Batteries"> Batteries </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes"> Electrodes </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291058&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Hollow structures"> Hollow structures </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292506&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Materials"> Materials </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292316&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Transition metals"> Transition metals </a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Binary+Metal&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_binary%20metal">binary metal</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Hollow+Structure&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_hollow%20structure">hollow structure</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Density+Functional+Theory&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_density%20functional%20theory">density functional theory</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Lithium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_lithium-ion%20batteries">lithium-ion batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium-ion%20batteries">sodium-ion batteries</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">1.  Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The development of alkali-ion-based rechargeable batteries is gaining huge academic interest. Among them, LIBs have become indispensable power sources for energy-related devices. Compared with the traditional batteries, LIBs possess many advantages such as long lifespan, portability, environmental friendliness, and so on. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref1 ref2" aria-label="reference 1 and 2">(1,2)</a> Nevertheless, the commercial anode material (graphite) only delivers a specific capacity of 372 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> for LIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref3" aria-label="reference 3">(3)</a> The limited storage performance of graphite cannot satisfy the eager requirements for high energy/power density devices. Simultaneously, the research on SIBs has gained sufficient momentum owing to their similar electrochemical mechanisms to LIBs and abundant sodium reserves. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref4 ref5" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref4 ref5" aria-label="reference 4 and 5">(4,5)</a> Unfortunately, the higher reduction potential (<i>E</i><sub>Na/Na</sub><sup>+</sup> = −2.7 V vs E<sub>Li/Li</sub><sup>+</sup> = −3.0 V) and the larger radius (1.02 Å for Na vs 0.76 Å for Li) usually result in the low energy density and poor cycle stability in SIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref6" aria-label="reference 6">(6)</a> The graphite presents nearly no capacity for SIBs. Therefore, more efficient anode materials with high capacities are greatly desired for LIBs and SIBs.</div><div class="NLM_p">Alloy-type materials are considered to be desirable anode candidates for LIBs and SIBs, which is attributed to their higher theoretical capacity induced by conversion and alloy reactions in comparison with carbonaceous materials. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7 ref8" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref7 ref8" aria-label="reference 7 and 8">(7,8)</a> Among them, Sn and the Sn-based materials (SnO<sub>2</sub>, SnO, SnS, etc.) have attracted considerable attention as anodes of LIBs and SIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9 ref10" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref9 ref10" aria-label="reference 9 and 10">(9,10)</a> However, the development of most Sn-based anode materials is hampered by two fatal factors. One is the intrinsic poor electrical conductivity, which result in sluggish reaction kinetics. The other is the severe volume expansion (≈300% for Li and ≈420% for Na) due to the formation of the alloy M<sub><i>x</i></sub>Sn (M = Li, Na) upon continued cycles, leading to the structure collapse and pulverization of the active material. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9 ref11 ref12" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref9 ref11 ref12" aria-label="reference 9, 11 and 12">(9,11,12)</a> Various strategies have been implemented to circumvent these issues. One feasible strategy is to engineer various structures, such as hollow rods, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref13" aria-label="reference 13">(13)</a> core–shell structures, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref14" aria-label="reference 14">(14)</a> nanosheets, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref15" aria-label="reference 15">(15)</a> and nanotubes, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref16" aria-label="reference 16">(16)</a> which is favorable to buffer the volume variation and prevent pulverization of electrodes. Combining Sn-based materials with carbonaceous materials has also been confirmed as an effective method to relieve the volume variation. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17 ref18" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref17 ref18" aria-label="reference 17 and 18">(17,18)</a> Zhao et al. fabricated SnS<sub>2</sub>/Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>-rGO delivering specific capacities of 845.7 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup> in LIBs and 392.9 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup> in SIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref17" aria-label="reference 17">(17)</a> Kuang et al. prepared a fibril-shaped MnOQD@CHNTs composite, which maintained high capacities of 392.8 and 223 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> for LIBs and SIBs, respectively. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref19" aria-label="reference 19">(19)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">In addition, the introduction of the second metal species has been proved to be a strategy that can improve the conductivity and enrich the redox reactions compared with their monometal counterparts. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref20" aria-label="reference 20">(20)</a> For example, Liu and co-workers presented a high performance anode of SIBs based on CoSnS<sub><i>x</i></sub>@NC (exceptionally long cycle life of 4000 cycles). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> Gao et al. developed CoMoO<sub>4</sub>@NC as an anode of SIBs, which exhibited a specific capacity of 190 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 3200 cycles. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref22" aria-label="reference 22">(22)</a> Monometal materials of Sn and Mn have shown promising performance as anodes of LIBs and SIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23 ref24" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref23 ref24" aria-label="reference 23 and 24">(23,24)</a> Moreover, a combination of Sn and Mn as a binary-metal active material will possess “metal-like conductivity”. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a> Therefore, a binary tin manganese metal compound will benefit from improved intrinsic conductivity, which is expected to become a pivotal factor in improving lithium and sodium storage performance.</div><div class="NLM_p last">In this work, hollow binary-metal Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC was constructed via hydrothermal treatments, carbon coating, and a subsequent high-temperature process. Until now, rare studies have reported that Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC acts as an anode material in LIBs. Besides, the Na storage behavior of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC is explored for the first time. The hollow structure coupling with carbon can provide adequate space to mitigate the strain and tolerate volume expansion/contraction. Additionally, introduction of heterogeneous species improves the conductivity of the material, which is beneficial to electron/ion transfer and speeds up the reaction kinetics. The LIBs with as-prepared Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC as the anode deliver high rate capability of 554.2 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 5000 mA g<sup>–1</sup> and excellent reversible capacity of 823.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 1000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. As the anode in SIBs, Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC delivers extended cycle life (a capacity of 185.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 7000 cycles at 2000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>). Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC has been studied as the anode in LIBs and SIBs, respectively, and it presents superb electrochemical performance in lithium and sodium storage.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">2.  Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4">2.1.  Structural Characterizations of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC</h3><div class="NLM_p"><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a> describes the overall fabricating process of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC. First, uniform and smooth ZnSn(OH)<sub>6</sub> cubes with an average size of 1 μm were facilely synthesized by coprecipitation of ZnCl<sub>2</sub>/SnCl<sub>4</sub> and etching of concentrated NaOH (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>). Afterward, ZnSn(OH)<sub>6</sub> was annealed in air to obtain Zn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>@SnO<sub>2</sub>, and Zn<sup>2+</sup> ions in Zn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub> were extracted by selective complexation to get pure SnO<sub>2</sub> crystals (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2a</a>). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a> Next, the MnO<sub>2</sub> nanosheets grew on the surface of SnO<sub>2</sub> to form SnO<sub>2</sub>@MnO<sub>2</sub>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref27" aria-label="reference 27">(27)</a> After assembling MnO<sub>2</sub>, a polydopamine (PDA) layer was coated on the as-prepared sample. Finally, Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC was obtained by annealing treatment under the protection of Ar. The reaction process of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC composite in the final step can be explored by the XRD and XPS analyses of comparative samples (Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC and SnO<sub>2</sub>@MnO<sub>2</sub>). As shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2b,c</a>, the XRD pattern shows that SnO<sub>2</sub> is converted to Sn and SnO<sub>2</sub> composite after carbon coating and calcination. The Sn 3d XPS spectrum of Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC also illustrates the coexistence of Sn<sup>4+</sup> and Sn<sup>0</sup>. So it can be deduced that the carbon derived from PDA serves as a reaction reduction agent during a high-temperature process. Combining the XRD and XPS characterizations of SnO<sub>2</sub>@MnO<sub>2</sub> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3</a>), the main reactions include three portions: First, PDA was converted to carbon in the high temperature. Subsequently, partial SnO<sub>2</sub> and MnO<sub>2</sub> of SnO<sub>2</sub>@MnO<sub>2</sub> were reduced to Sn and MnO, which obtained the products of Sn, SnO<sub>2</sub>, and MnO. Finally, the unreduced SnO<sub>2</sub> and MnO underwent a solid-phase reaction to form Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub> under high temperature, and the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC composite was obtained. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref29" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref28 ref29" aria-label="reference 28 and 29">(28,29)</a></div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/large/am1c08632_0002.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. Schematic diagram of the synthesis route of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/large/am1c08632_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c08632&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">SEM and TEM characterizations were performed to carefully analyze the microstructure and the morphology of samples. As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>a,b, SnO<sub>2</sub> with a 160 nm outer wall thickness is obtained after processing ZnSn(OH)<sub>6</sub>. The surface of SnO<sub>2</sub> becomes rough and porous compared with a ZnSn(OH)<sub>6</sub> cube, but its cubic morphology and hollow structure are well inherited. After the hydrothermal reaction of KMnO<sub>4</sub>, MnO<sub>2</sub> nanosheets successfully grow on the external side of the SnO<sub>2</sub> precursor as mentioned above (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>c,d). In the ultimate procedure, the MnO<sub>2</sub> nanosheets with SnO<sub>2</sub> evolve into Sn and Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub> composite. A typical FESEM image of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC composite shows a cube-like morphology and the hollow interiors can be obviously found in the corresponding TEM image (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>e,f). The high-resolution TEM image in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>g displays that Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC transforms into a hollow cube embedded with Sn and Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub> nanoparticles (a size of about 15 nm). The binary-metal Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub> nanoparticles and Sn are wrapped with a carbon layer (a thickness of 20 nm). The enlarged HRTEM images of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC composite are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>h,i, in which the lattice fringes with a spacing of 0.51 and 0.25 nm correspond to the (111) and (222) planes of Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>, respectively. In addition, the marked lattice fringe distance of 0.38 nm corresponds to the (101) plane of Sn. The element mapping images (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>j) prove that Sn, Mn, O, C, and N elements are uniformly distributed throughout the whole hollow cube. Combining the results discussed above, it can be believed that the final Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC composite is composed of Sn, Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub> nanoparticles, as well as N-doped carbon, which are confined in a cubic frame.</div><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/large/am1c08632_0003.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. Structure and morphology characterizations. (a) FESEM image and (b) TEM image of SnO<sub>2</sub>. (c) FESEM image and (d) TEM image of SnO<sub>2</sub>@MnO<sub>2</sub>. (e) FESEM image and (f, g) TEM images of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC. (h, i) HRTEM images and (j) EDS mapping (Sn, Mn, O, C, and N) of the hollow Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/large/am1c08632_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c08632&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The XRD pattern of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC is shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>a, which demonstrates four planes (labeled purple) corresponding to the presence of Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub> (JCPDS NO. 74-2378). While all of the other peaks labeled green are well indexed to Sn (JCPDS NO. 86-2264). The Raman characterization of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC was conducted to further verify the existence of the carbon matrix (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>b). The characteristic peaks of the D-band (1342 cm<sup>–1</sup>) and the G-band (1566 cm<sup>–1</sup>) represent disordered carbon and graphite of sp<sup>2</sup> hybridization, respectively. The intensity ratio of the D- and G-band signals, namely, <i>I</i><sub>D</sub>/<i>I</i><sub>G</sub>, is 0.98, demonstrating that the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC material has partial graphitization and good conductivity. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref30" aria-label="reference 30">(30)</a> The N<sub>2</sub> adsorption/desorption measurement was performed as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>c. Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC exhibits the isothermal curve of IV type and the hysteresis loop of H3, which is related to the characterizations of the mesoporous. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref31" aria-label="reference 31">(31)</a> The specific surface area (SSA) of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC is calculated as 44.81 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>–1</sup> by the Brunauer–Emmett–Teller (BET) analysis. In addition, the corresponding pore size distribution curve shows the presence of a large number of mesopores (inset of <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>c). The mesoporous/total pore volume ratio is calculated as 83.44% for Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC. Such a SSA and mesoporous volume ratio are conducive to improve the cycle stability of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref32" aria-label="reference 32">(32)</a></div><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/large/am1c08632_0004.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. Crystal structure and composition characterizations. (a) XRD pattern, (b) Raman spectrum, and (c) N<sub>2</sub> sorption/desorption isotherms (inset: pore size distribution) of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC. XPS spectra of (d) Sn 3d, (e) Mn 2p, and (f) C 1s of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/large/am1c08632_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c08632&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p last">The chemical states of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC composite were explored by XPS measurements. The XPS spectrum of Sn 3d is displayed in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>d. The Sn 3d spectrum exhibits four peaks: two peaks located at 495.0 and 486.6 eV can be explained to Sn 3d<sub>3/2</sub> and Sn 3d<sub>5/2</sub> orbitals of tetravalent Sn<sup>4+</sup> from Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>. Meanwhile, the shoulder peaks at 493.2 and 484.8 eV correspond to Sn 3d<sub>3/2</sub> and Sn 3d<sub>5/2</sub> of metallic Sn<sup>0</sup>, which agree well with the reported results of Sn and Sn<sup>4+</sup>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref2 ref33" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref2 ref33" aria-label="reference 2 and 33">(2,33)</a> These results further confirm the reduction of partial Sn<sup>4+</sup> to Sn<sup>0</sup> by high-temperature carbothermal reduction. As for Mn 2p (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>e), two peaks at 653.3 and 641.5 eV are associated with the spin orbits of bivalent Mn<sup>2+</sup>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref34" aria-label="reference 34">(34)</a> Additionally, the two typical satellite peaks at 657.4 and 645.6 eV can be seen in Mn<sup>2+</sup> systems. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref35 ref36" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref35 ref36" aria-label="reference 35 and 36">(35,36)</a> The O 1s XPS spectrum of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC presents three peaks at 529.2, 531.9, and 532.9 eV (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6a</a>), corresponding to the lattice oxygen Mn–O, Sn–O, and C═O, respectively. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref2 ref36" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref2 ref36" aria-label="reference 2 and 36">(2,36)</a> As presented in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>f for the C 1s spectrum, the signals of C–C-hybridized carbon, C–N bond, and C═O bond can be found at 284.4, 285.9, and 288.5 eV. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref37" aria-label="reference 37">(37)</a> Meanwhile, the N 1s XPS spectrum of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6b</a>) presents three N peaks. The peaks include pyridinic N, pyrrolic N, and graphitic N, which are located at 398.4, 399.8, and 400.7 eV, respectively. The N content is from the inherent nitrogen-containing organic ligands in PDA. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref38 ref39" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref38 ref39" aria-label="reference 38 and 39">(38,39)</a> The EDS elemental mapping was performed to determine the specific content of metal (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7</a>). The result shows that the atomic ratio of Sn to Mn is 51.7:48.3, allowing the calculation of the molar ratio of Sn and Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub> in the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC system to be 1:0.93. TGA was conducted from 40 to 700 °C under an air condition (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S8</a>). According to the weight loss percentage and EDS analysis results of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC, the contents of Sn, Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>, and carbon are concluded to be 17.6, 40.7, and 41.7%, respectively.</div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5">2.2.  Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC for Lithium-Ion Batteries</h3><div class="NLM_p">To evaluate the potential lithium storage performance, the electrochemical measurements of a Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC composite as an anode were performed in the CR2032 coin-type cells. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>a shows the cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC between 0.01 and 3.0 V. For the initial cathodic process, three reduction peaks can be identified. The peak at around 0.62 V may be attributed to the decomposition of Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub> (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq1" aria-label="eq 1">eq </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq1" aria-label="1">1</a>). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref40" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref40" aria-label="reference 40">(40)</a> The peak at about 0.53 V is associated with the formation of an irreversible solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) film. The peak (0.16 V) can be attributed to the alloying reaction of the metal Sn and Li (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq2" aria-label="eq 2">eq </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq2" aria-label="2">2</a>). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9 ref35 ref41" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref9 ref35 ref41" aria-label="reference 9, 35 and 41">(9,35,41)</a> During the initial anodic process, the oxidation peaks correspond to the multistep dealloying reactions of Li<sub><i>x</i></sub>Sn (0.5–1.1 V) and oxidation reactions (1.26 V) of Sn<sup>0</sup>/Mn<sup>0</sup> to Sn<sup>2+</sup>/Mn<sup>2+</sup> (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq3" aria-label="eqs 3">eqs </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq3" aria-label="3">3</a> and <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq4" aria-label="4">4</a>). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref40" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref40" aria-label="reference 40">(40)</a> In particular, the obvious oxidation peak (2.1 V) in the curves gradually enhances with the cycles going on due to the further oxidation of Mn<sup>2+</sup>, which can provide additional specific capacity for the subsequent reaction processes. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref42 ref43 ref44" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref42 ref43 ref44" aria-label="reference 42 to 44">(42−44)</a> In the subsequent discharge process, the peaks at 1.2 and 0.43 V are referenced to the reduction of SnO<sub>2</sub> and MnO, respectively. The discharge/charge reactions are also discussed by ex situ XRD characterizations after discharge and charge (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S9a</a>). When Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC is fully discharged to 0.01 V, the peaks of Mn and Li<sub><i>x</i></sub>Sn emerge. Once fully charged, the peaks of SnO<sub>2</sub> and MnO<sub><i>x</i></sub> appear, while the peaks of Mn and Li<sub><i>x</i></sub>Sn disappear. The redox peaks from the second cycle onward can be distinguished from those of the first cycle, but the CV curves of the 2nd and 3rd cycle almost overlap, proving the good reversibility of Li intercalation/deintercalation and cycling stability. Accordingly, the relevant electrochemical reactions of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC with lithium ions are listed as follows <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref35" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref35" aria-label="reference 35">(35)</a><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq1"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_m001.gif" alt="" id="_i6"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(1)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq2"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_m002.gif" alt="" id="_i7"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(2)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq3"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_m003.gif" alt="" id="_i8"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(3)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq4"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_m004.gif" alt="" id="_i9"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(4)</span></div></div></span></div><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/large/am1c08632_0005.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. Electrochemical performance for LIBs. (a) Initial CV curves of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode at 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. (b) Cycling performance at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup> and (c) rate capabilities from 100 to 5000 mA g<sup>–1</sup> of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC and Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC (inset: specific capacity retention). (d) Rate capability comparison of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode with the previous literature. (e) Long-term cycling performance of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode at 1000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. (f) Cycle performance comparison of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode with Sn/Mn-based materials. (g) EIS spectra after 100 cycles (inset: equivalent circuit model) and (h) enlarged EIS spectra of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC and Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC electrodes (inset: the summaries of <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>).</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/large/am1c08632_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c08632&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p"><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>b shows the cycle performance of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC and Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC electrodes at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC exhibits an initial discharge capacity of 1338.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with an initial Coulombic efficiency (CE) of 73.88%. Due to the better intrinsic conductivity, Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC maintains much higher discharge capacity (1039.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>) compared with Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC (469.1 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>), as well as about 99% CE after the 2nd cycle. In addition to the high capacity, the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC anode shows excellent rate capability (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>c). Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC delivers average discharge capacities of 1022.1, 910.4, 825.7, 755.0, 680.2, and 554.2 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> in a current density range of 100–5000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. After 60 cycles at various rates, the specific capacity is restored to 976.6 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup> and the specific capacity retention is 95.5% (inset of <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>c). In contrast, the Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC electrode shows poor average specific capacities of 1136.3, 914.2, 742.8, 596.8, 461.7, and 312.6 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> under the same conditions. Moreover, the Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC electrode only retains a capacity of 578.3 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup> with a capacity retention rate of 50.9%. The higher capacity and superior rate retention of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode are assigned to the enhanced electronic conductivity, resulting in the rapid transfer of Li<sup>+</sup>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref38" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref38" aria-label="reference 38">(38)</a> Additionally, the rate performance comparison with the previously reported Sn/Mn-based materials is shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>d. The long-term cycling lifespan of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode is also assessed at large current densities. The Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode maintains a reversible specific capacity of 823.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 600 cycles at 1000 mA g<sup>–1</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>e). In contrast, solid structure Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC (labeled as Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC(s)) and SnO<sub>2</sub>@MnO<sub>2</sub> deliver specific capacities of 823.8 and 294.1 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively, lower than that of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S10a</a>). Some fluctuation phenomena in the capacity of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode can be found due to the combined effect of SEI cracking/reforming and activation of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode during the cycling process. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref45" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref45" aria-label="reference 45">(45)</a> When carrying out the cycling stability test at larger current density (2000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>), the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode delivers a reversible capacity of 550.2 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 1000 cycles (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S11</a>). Due to the buffer of the hollow structure, Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC and Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC electrodes (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S12a,b</a>) still maintain the cubic structure to a certain extent. Taken together, the outstanding Li storage performance of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC can give the credit to the joint effect of the hollow structure, carbon components, and the introduction of Mn heterogeneous species. The cyclic performance of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode is superior to most recently published related electrode materials (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>f). Moreover, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a> provides a comparison of the cyclic stability of binary-metal Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC with the previously reported monometal Sn/Mn-based materials. It can be clearly seen that the cyclic performance of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC is superior to that of the reported monometal Sn/Mn-based materials, implying that combination of binary-metal Sn/Mn improves the intrinsic conductivity and enhances the cyclic stability.</div><div class="NLM_p last">The enhanced rate capability and cyclic performance of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode in Li<sup>+</sup> storage can be assigned to the rapid transfer of charge, which can be verified by the EIS measurements. As displayed in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>g, the depressed semicircles in the high- and medium-frequency regions represent SEI impedance (<i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub>) and charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>), respectively. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref46 ref47" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref46 ref47" aria-label="reference 46 and 47">(46,47)</a> To observe the EIS profiles of electrodes more clearly, the enlarged EIS spectra are displayed in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>h. The <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC and Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC electrodes are summarized in the inset of <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>h. It is obvious that resistances of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode are smaller than those of Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC. This result indicates that the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode possesses enhanced conductivity and effective charge transfer, which lead to the improvement of electrochemical performance. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref48" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref48" aria-label="reference 48">(48)</a> It is well known that the SEI has an important impact on the electrochemical kinetics of anode materials. To get insight into the detailed chemical components of the SEI film on the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode, the XPS tests after one cycle lithiation were required (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S13a,b</a>). For the C 1s XPS spectrum, alkyl components and carbonates are found in the C 1s XPS signals at 284.5 eV (C–C/C–H), 286.2 eV (C–O), 288.9 eV (C═O), and 289.6 eV (CO<sub>3</sub>). The F 1s XPS spectrum exhibits two major signals at 684.2 and 687.3 eV, which represent LiF and LiPF<sub>6</sub>, respectively. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref49 ref50" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref49 ref50" aria-label="reference 49 and 50">(49,50)</a></div></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i10" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i10">2.3.  Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC for Sodium-Ion Batteries</h3><div class="NLM_p">The Na storage performance of a Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC anode was also investigated, and is illustrated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>. The CV curves of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC are displayed in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>a. In the first cathodic scan, the broad peak of 0.9–1.2 V is assigned to the decomposition of Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub> (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq5" aria-label="eq 5">eq </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq5" aria-label="5">5</a>) and the generation of an irreversible SEI layer.
