The other peak at 0.07 V corresponds to the formation of alloy Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Sn (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq6" aria-label="eq 6">eq </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq6" aria-label="6">6</a>). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref51" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref51" aria-label="reference 51">(51)</a> In the initial anodic scan, the peaks ranging from 0.3 to 0.9 V are related to the desodiation processes of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Sn. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref52 ref53" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref52 ref53" aria-label="reference 52 and 53">(52,53)</a> The other two small peaks at 1.14 and 2.0 V are attributed to the oxidation of Sn and Mn, respectively (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq7" aria-label="eqs 7">eqs </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq7" aria-label="7">7</a> and <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq8" aria-label="8">8</a>). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref54 ref55" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref54 ref55" aria-label="reference 54 and 55">(54,55)</a><a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S9b</a> shows the XRD patterns of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode after discharge and charge. The peaks of Mn and Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Sn can be found at the state of discharge to 0.01 V, indicating the intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup>. When the anode is charged at 3.0 V, the signals of SnO<sub>2</sub> and MnO appear. However, redox peak positions of subsequent cycles shift slightly because of the decomposition of the electrolyte and the rearrangement of the structure. The CVs are almost overlapped from 7th cycle, suggesting the reversible sodiation/desodiation. The electrochemical reactions can be summarized as the following process <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref56" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref56" aria-label="reference 56">(56)</a><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq5"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_m005.gif" alt="" id="_i11"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(5)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq6"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_m006.gif" alt="" id="_i12"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(6)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq7"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_m007.gif" alt="" id="_i13"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(7)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq8"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_m008.gif" alt="" id="_i14"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(8)</span></div></div></span></div><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/large/am1c08632_0006.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. Electrochemical performance for SIBs. (a) Initial CV curves of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode at 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. (b) Cycling performance at 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup> and (c) rate capabilities of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC and Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC (inset: specific capacity retention) from 50 to 2000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. (d) Rate capability comparison of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode with Sn/Mn-based anodes in the previous literature. (e) Long-term cycling performance at 2000 mA g<sup>–1</sup> of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode. (f) Cycle performance comparison of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode with Sn/Mn-based materials. (g) EIS spectra of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC under different cycles (inset: the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of different cycles). (h) EIS spectra of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC and Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC electrodes (inset: equivalent circuit model).</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/large/am1c08632_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c08632&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The cycle performances of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC and Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC electrodes are displayed in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>b. The capacities of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode reached 320.1 and 500 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> for the first charge and discharge, which corresponds to 64.01% initial CE. It still maintains a reversible capacity of 279.1 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 100 cycles at 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, which is superior to that of the Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC electrode (184.4 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>). Moreover, the CE of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode can remain almost 98% after the 13th cycle. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>c shows the rate capabilities comparison of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC and Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC electrodes at rates of 50, 100, 200, 500, 1000, and 2000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. With increasing rate, the corresponding average capacities of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode are 313.4, 265.1, 250.3, 227.3, 200.4, and 165.3 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>. As the rate reduces to 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, it can recover to 264.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with a specific capacity retention of 84.4% (inset in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>c). On the contrary, the Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC electrode delivers low capacity and inferior capacity retention (70.3%). The rate performance of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode for SIBs remains advantageous compared with other Sn/Mn-based anode materials previously reported, especially in terms of high rates (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>d), which is attributed to the excellent conductivity originating from the synergy of binary-metal Sn and Mn.</div><div class="NLM_p last"><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>e shows long-term cycling lifespan of a Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode at 2000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC retains a stable reversible capacity of 185.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 7000 cycles, which has better cyclic performance than most recently published Sn/Mn-based materials (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>f and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a>). Additionally, it can be found that the capacity shows a continuous increase until 2000 cycles, which can be explained by EIS analysis. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>g shows EIS spectra of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC under 100, 300, 500, 1000, and 2000 cycles. The corresponding resistances (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) are calculated to be 235.3, 128.3, 92.8, 35.5, and 26.1 Ω by the equivalent circuit (inset of <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>h). It can be seen that the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> value gradually decreases before 2000 cycles, indicating that the increase of capacity in the first 2000 cycles is originated from the gradual activation of the active material and the generation of a polymer/gel SEI. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref57" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref57" aria-label="reference 57">(57)</a> The XPS spectra of the SEI film are shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S13c,d</a> for SIBs. The characteristic peaks of sp<sup>2</sup> carbon (284.5 eV), CH<sub>2</sub>– (285.4 eV), C–O (286.6 eV), C═O (288.6 eV), and CO<sub>3</sub> (289.6 eV) can be observed. Among them, the peaks of C–O and C═O are typical organic components of the SEI. The signal of CO<sub>3</sub> corresponds to the carbonate group (inorganics Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>), which is a ubiquitous decomposition byproduct of a carbonate electrolyte. Also, the F 1s XPS spectrum displays the existence of NaF. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref58" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref58" aria-label="reference 58">(58)</a> Meanwhile, the cycling performance tests of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC, Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC(s), and SnO<sub>2</sub>@MnO<sub>2</sub> were also conducted at 4000 mA g<sup>–1</sup> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S10b</a>). The Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode showed a discharge capacity of 169.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 3000 cycles. In contrast, the specific capacities of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC(s) and SnO<sub>2</sub>@MnO<sub>2</sub> are 147.7 and 34.9 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. Among them, SnO<sub>2</sub>@MnO<sub>2</sub> basically has no capacity contribution for SIBs. The structure and the morphology of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC and Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC electrodes after cycles were investigated and are shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S12c,d</a>. According to the abovementioned analysis results, it is confirmed that the electrochemical performance of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC as a SIB anode is enhanced by the introduction of a hollow structure, carbon networks, as well as the Mn heterogeneous species. The Nyquist plots of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC and Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC electrodes after 10 cycles at 2000 mA g<sup>–1</sup> are obtained by EIS spectra and are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>h. The Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode exhibits smaller <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> (269.4 Ω) compared with the Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC electrode (575 Ω) due to the higher electronic conductivity of a binary-metal composite in comparison with a monometal composite. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref59 ref60" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref59 ref60" aria-label="reference 59 and 60">(59,60)</a></div></div><div id="sec2_4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i15" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i15">2.4.  Kinetic Analyses for Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC</h3><div class="NLM_p">The kinetics mechanism of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC in LIBs and SIBs was investigated by CV measurements. As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>a, as the sweep rate increases, the shape of CV profiles remains essentially unchanged. But the cathodic peak positions move slightly toward low potential and the anodic peaks shift to high potential, implying the slight polarization of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode. The relationship of the peak current (<i>i</i>) and the scan rate (<i>v</i>) can be fitted by the following equations to confirm the energy storage mechanism<span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq9"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_m009.gif" alt="" id="_i16"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(9)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq10"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_m010.gif" alt="" id="_i17"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(10)</span></div></div></span>where <i>a</i> and <i>b</i> are empirical parameters. The value of <i>b</i> is equal to 0.5, which represents diffusion-controlled redox reaction processes. When the <i>b</i> value is about 1.0, the energy storage process is a capacitance-dominated process. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref61" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref61" aria-label="reference 61">(61)</a> In <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>b, the <i>b</i> values of peak I, II, and III are calculated to be 0.85, 0.84, and 0.86, respectively. All <i>b</i> values are between 0.5 and 1.0, demonstrating that the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC energy storage process is a mixed kinetics reaction process (controlled by both surface capacitive and diffusion) in LIBs. The capacitance contribution to the total capacity can be quantitatively obtained by <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq11" aria-label="eq 11">eq </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq11" aria-label="11">11</a><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq11"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_m011.gif" alt="" id="_i18"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(11)</span></div></div></span>where <i>k</i><sub>1</sub><i>v</i> and <i>k</i><sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> are the pseudocapacitive and diffusion-controlled currents, respectively. As shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S14a</a> and <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>c, the contribution of pseudocapacitive to the total current for LIBs gradually increases from 58.1 to 87.6% with the increment of the sweep rate, revealing fast charge transfer. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref62" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref62" aria-label="reference 62">(62)</a> Moreover, the electrochemical kinetics mechanism of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC for SIBs was also explored by corresponding kinetic analyses (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>d). Similar to the LIBs, the appearance of the CV curves is maintained with increasing scan rate. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>e shows that <i>b</i> values of peaks I, II, and III are 0.83, 0.94, and 0.89 for three redox peaks marked in pink, implying that the electrochemical reaction of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC is mainly pseudocapacitive-controlled in SIBs. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>f displays that the capacitive contribution ratio gradually goes up from 61.8 to 88.9%. The capacity of about 88.9% is assigned to capacitive contribution at 2.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S14b</a>). The enhanced capacitive behavior indicates great reaction kinetics of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC for LIBs and SIBs. Furthermore, the capacitive contribution ratio in SIBs is higher than the value of LIBs at the same scanning speed. This phenomenon can be ascribed to the larger radius of Na<sup>+</sup> compared with Li<sup>+</sup>, impeding its insertion into the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC composite. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref63" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref63" aria-label="reference 63">(63)</a></div><figure id="fig6" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_0007.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/large/am1c08632_0007.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. Kinetics investigation of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC. (a) CV curves at various scan rates (I, II, III: specific redox peaks). (b) Plots of Log(<i>v</i>) against Log(<i>i</i>) and (c) contribution ratios of the pseudocapacitive- and diffusion-controlled capacity at different scan rates for LIBs. (d) CV curves at various scan rates (I, II, III: specific redox peaks), (e) plots of Log(<i>v</i>) against Log(<i>i</i>), and (<i>f</i>) contribution ratios of the pseudocapacitive- and diffusion-controlled capacity at different scan rates for SIBs.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/large/am1c08632_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c08632&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">To gain further insight into the mechanism of enhanced electrochemical storage, DFT calculation was performed. The crystal structures of Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub> and Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub> are constructed to study the effect of introducing the second metal species on the electronic structure at the atomic level (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>). It is worth noting that carbon is not included in the DFT calculations to verify whether the conductivity of the bimetallic material is better than that of the corresponding monometallic material. According to the performed calculation, the introduction of Mn species leads to an increase in the density of energy levels at the Fermi level. The increased density-of-states (DOS) at the Fermi level demonstrates the higher electronic conductivity in the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub> system, which is more conducive to charge diffusion kinetics. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref64" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref64" aria-label="reference 64">(64)</a></div><figure id="fig7" data-index="7" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 7</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/medium/am1c08632_0008.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/large/am1c08632_0008.jpeg" id="gr7" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 7. Crystal structure and corresponding density-of-states for (a, b) Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub> and (c, d) Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>. Tin atoms are marked with gray, manganese atoms with purple, and oxygen atoms with red.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/asset/images/large/am1c08632_0008.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c08632&amp;id=fig7"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i19">3.  Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In summary, a hollow Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC composite was designed and fabricated via multistep hydrothermal reactions, polydopamine encapsulation, and a high-temperature carbonization process. The existence of binary metals (Sn and Mn) increases the DOS at the Fermi level, improves the conductivity, and accelerates the charge transfer kinetics through a Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC electrode, thereby endowing a Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC anode with impressive cycle life. When employed as an anode for lithium storage, the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC anode exhibits a high specific capacity of 1039.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> for 100 cycles at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, good rate capability of 554.2 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 5000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, and stable cycle performance (823.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 600 cycles at 1000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>). Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC is used as an anode in SIBs for the first time. It delivers a superior reversible capacity of 279.1 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> for 100 cycles at 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. Specifically, even when performing at a large current density of 2000 mA g<sup>–1</sup> for 7000 charging and discharging cycles, the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC composite still possesses a reversible capacity of 185.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>. This work emphasizes the prominent position of binary-metal materials in energy storage, paving the way for breakthroughs in the field of energy storage.</div></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i20">4.  Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec4_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i21" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i21">4.1.  Syntheses of Hollow SnO<sub>2</sub> and SnO<sub>2</sub>@MnO<sub>2</sub></h3><div class="NLM_p last">ZnSn(OH)<sub>6</sub> hollow/solid cubes were prepared based on a previously reported method. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref65" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref65" aria-label="reference 65">(65)</a> ZnSn(OH)<sub>6</sub> was annealed in air at 600 °C for 4 h to obtain a Zn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>/SnO<sub>2</sub> composite material. Next, the mixed solution of 20 mM Zn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>/SnO<sub>2</sub> and 90 mM ethylene diamine tetraacetic acid (EDTA) was prepared and stirred for 30 min. The mixture was heated up to 220 °C for 12 h to get hollow and solid SnO<sub>2</sub>. Then, 100 mg of as-prepared SnO<sub>2</sub> and 200 mg of KMnO<sub>4</sub> were dissolved in 60 mL of DIW. Subsequently, a certain amount of 37% HCl was dropped into the abovementioned solution. After stirring for a period of time, the solution was poured into an autoclave reactor (90 mL capacity) and the temperature was increased to 120 °C for 6 h. After the autoclave was cooled, the resulting powder SnO<sub>2</sub>@MnO<sub>2</sub> was finally obtained.</div></div><div id="sec4_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i22" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i22">4.2.  Syntheses of Hollow Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC, Solid Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC(s), and Hollow Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC</h3><div class="NLM_p last">A total of 100 mg of synthesized SnO<sub>2</sub>@MnO<sub>2</sub> was dispersed in a 10 mM Tris buffer solution. The pH of the solution was adjusted to ∼8.5 by HCl and the suspension was treated by sonication for 10 min. Next, 100 mg of dopamine hydrochloride was dissolved into the abovementioned mixture and reacted for 12 h. In this process, the polydopamine (PDA) layer self-polymerized on SnO<sub>2</sub>@MnO<sub>2</sub> to form a SnO<sub>2</sub>@MnO<sub>2</sub>@PDA composite. Finally, the obtained SnO<sub>2</sub>@MnO<sub>2</sub>@PDA was annealed at 600 °C and kept for 2 h to get the final product Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC. For comparative research, the solid Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC(s) was fabricated with the same method by the solid ZnSn(OH)<sub>6</sub> precursor. The hollow Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC composite was synthesized with the same method except for the adding of KMnO<sub>4</sub>.</div></div><div id="sec4_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i23" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i23">4.3.  Material Characterizations</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The power XRD characterizations were conducted using a Brucker D8 advance X-ray diffractometer spectrometer (Cu Kα radiation, λ = 1.5406  Å). The chemical surface component and the chemical bonding state of the samples were characterized by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) with Al Kα radiation. The morphology and the structure of the samples were obtained using a field-emission scanning electron microscope (FESEM, Zeiss SIGMA) and a transmission electron microscope (TEM, JEM-2010 HT). High-resolution transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM) and corresponding EDS were conducted on a JEM-F200 microscope at 200 kV. The specific surface area and porosity property were measured on a JW-BK 100 analyzer. The Raman spectrum was collected using a laser confocal microRaman spectrometer (RenishawinVia, Renishaw). Thermogravimetric analysis (TGA, Mettler-Toledo, Switzerland) was performed in an air atmosphere.</div></div><div id="sec4_4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i24" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i24">4.4.  Electrochemical Measurements</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The CR2032 coin-type cells were assembled in a Mikrouna glovebox (H<sub>2</sub>O and O<sub>2</sub> ≤0.01 ppm) to test as-prepared samples. First, a homogeneous slurry was made by mixing active materials, super P (conductivity agent), and polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF, binder) with a mass ratio of 7:2:1 in an <i>N</i>-methyl pyrrolidone (NMP) solvent. Then, the working electrodes were prepared by coating the formed slurry on a copper foil and punching the copper foil into round pieces with a diameter of 12 mm. The loading mass of each electrode disc was controlled in the range of 0.8–1.2 mg cm<sup>–1</sup> by adjusting the thickness of the electrode. For the LIBs, a lithium metal foil (Aladdin) was used as a counter electrode and 1 M LiPF<sub>6</sub> was dissolved in a mixed solvent of ethylene carbonate (EC) and diethyl carbonate (DEC) as an electrolyte. For the SIBs, a sodium metal foil (Aladdin) was used as a counter electrode and the electrolyte consisted of 1 M NaClO<sub>4</sub> in EC, dimethyl carbonate (DMC), and 5% fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC). The galvanostatic charge/discharge (GCD) tests were operated on a LAND-CT2001 battery test system under a charging/discharging voltage of 0.01–3.0 V. The CV profiles (in the voltage window of 0.01–3.0 V) and EIS spectra (in a frequency range of 10<sup>–2</sup>–10<sup>5</sup> Hz) were recorded by a CHI 760E electrochemical workstation (Shanghai Chenhua, China).</div></div><div id="sec4_5" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i25" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i25">4.5.  Theoretical Calculations</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The first-principles calculations about electronic density-of-states (DOS) were conducted using the Vienna Ab initio Simulation Package (VASP). The exchange–correlation energy functional was modeled by the generalized gradient approximation (GGA) and projector augmented wave (PAW). The energy cutoff was chosen to be 450 eV and the Monkhorst–Pack of <i>k</i>-points with a 4 × 6 × 9 grid was used to sample the Brillouin zone.</div></div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i26">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsami.1c08632?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.1c08632</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">XRD and SEM images of the ZnSn(OH)<sub>6</sub> precursor; the XRD pattern of SnO<sub>2</sub>; XRD and XPS profiles of SnO<sub>2</sub>@MnO<sub>2</sub>; XRD, XPS, SEM, and TEM profiles of Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC; SEM-EDS mapping, TGA and XPS characterizations of Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC; TEM images of the solid structure SnO<sub>2</sub> and Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC(s); XRD and SEM images of the Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC and Sn@SnO<sub>2</sub>-NC electrodes after charge/discharge cycles; XPS data of SEI; additional electrochemical tests for Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC, SnO<sub>2</sub>@MnO<sub>2</sub>, and Sn@Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>-NC(s) electrodes; and cycling performance comparisons (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c08632/suppl_file/am1c08632_si_001.pdf">am1c08632_si_001.pdf (1.24 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.1c08632" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget" style="display: block;"></div><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="85b54935-30e9-4058-a6d2-0b40fb754a85" class="mb-4">

                        cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Dual-carbon coupled Co5.47N composites for capacitive lithium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qian, Xukun; Wang, Hao; Wang, Ruirui; Zhang, Lilei; Li, Mingming; Zhou, Yong-Ning; Wu, Renbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">587</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">192-201</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCISA5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0021-9797</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal nitrides are of great interest as potential anodes for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) owing to their high theor. capacity.  However, poor cycling stability and rate performance greatly hinder their practical applications.  To better alleviate these problems, a unique 3D hierarchical nanocomposite constructed by dual carbon-coated Co5.47N nano-grains wrapped with carbon and reduced graphene oxide (Co5.47N@C@rGO) was synthesized through one-step simultaneous nitridation and carbonization of zeolitic imidazolate frameworks@GO precursor.  The 3D hierarchical Co5.47N@C@rGO composite can combine the good cond. and mech. strength of rGO and a high theor. capacity of Co5.47N.  When explored as anode material for LIBs, Co5.47N@C@rGO exhibits a high reversible capacity of ∼860 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 1.0 A g-1 after 500 cycles and excellent high-rate capability (665 and 573 mAh g-1 at current densities of 3.2 and 6.4 A g-1, resp.).  The excellent electrochem. performance of Co5.47N@C@rGO can be ascribed to its hierarchically porous structure and the synergistic effect between Co5.47N nano-grains and rGO.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref2" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2020.154579"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, F.                         cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Yolk-shelled Sn@C@MnO hierarchical hybrid nanospheres for high performance lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Fanchao; Wang, Yong; Guo, Wenbin; Mao, Peiyuan; Rao, Shun; Xiao, Pandeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">829</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">154579</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JALCEU</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0925-8388</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metallic tin exhibits great potential as an alternative to com. graphite anode materials.  However, its tremendous vol. change during cycles leads to significant capacity fading, which hampers its practical application.  In this work, Sn nanoparticles are confined to a carbon nanocage to form Sn@C@MnO yolk-shell hierarchical hybrid nanospheres as anode nanomaterials for Li-ion battery.  In the novel nanostructures, the yolk-shell nanostructures can well buffer the vol. contraction/expansion of Sn nanocores during cycles; the carbon shell can provide high cond. and inhibit Sn and MnO nanocrystals from stacking; MnO nanocrystals on the C shell can not only offer sufficient active sites for Li-ion adsorption, but also validly consolidate the structural stability of the shell in the yolk-shell nanostructure.  Benefiting from the unique nanostructures, Sn@C@MnO yolk-shell hierarchical hybrid nanospheres exhibit superior electrochem. lithium storage performances (822 mAhg-1 after 250 cycles at 0.1Ag-1) and long-term cyclic stability (603mAhg-1 after 500 cycles at 0.5Ag-1).  This work offers valuable insight into the synthetic strategy of Sn-based anode materials with novel hierarchical hybrid nanostructures.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref3" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1016/j.matlet.2019.126827"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Three-Dimensional Porous Sn/NC Spheres with Outstanding Properties for Lithium Ion Battery</span>. <i>Mater.                 10.1016/j.matlet.2019.126827</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D259%26publication_year%3D2020%26journal%3DMater.%2BLett.%26author%3DW.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BDu%26author%3DJ.%2BQian%26author%3DF.%2BChen%26title%3DThree-Dimensional%2BPorous%2BSn%252FNC%2BSpheres%2Bwith%2BOutstanding%2BProperties%2Bfor%2BLithium%2BIon%2BBattery%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.matlet.2019.126827&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c08632&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.matlet.2019.126827&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-dimensional porous Sn/NC spheres with outstanding properties for lithium ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Wenyu; Du, Zeru; Qian, Junchao; Chen, Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Letters</span>

                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MLETDJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0167-577X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Three-dimensional hierarchical sphere with Sn quantum dot decorated on the porous N-doped C framework (NC) is successfully prepd. via a simple spray drying process and subsequent calcination treatment.  The porous Sn/NC composite displays outstanding properties for Li ion battery with a large capacity of 589 mA-h g-1 and robust stability.  This may result from the synergistic effect between the porous structure, the C network and Sn quantum-dots, which can cushion the vol. expansion of the electrode material.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref4" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1016/j.apsusc.2020.148033"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Narsimulu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nagaraju, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chandra
Sekhar, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ramulu, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su Yu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Three-Dimensional Porous SnO<sub>2</sub>/Carbon Cloth Electrodes for High-Performance Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Appl.                         cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-dimensional porous SnO2/carbon cloth electrodes for high-performance lithium- and sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Narsimulu, D.; Nagaraju, Goli; Chandra Sekhar, S.; Ramulu, Bhimanaboina; Su Yu, Jae</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Surface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">538</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">148033</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ASUSEE</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0169-4332</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The tin oxide nanoparticles (SnO2-NPs) were successfully synthesized on the conductive carbon cloth (CC) using a simple one-step solvothermal method to form three-dimensional (3D) porous SnO2/CC composite.  The SnO2-NPs were uniformly deposited on CC and fine pores existed between the SnO2-NPs.  The synthesized 3D porous SnO2/CC composite was investigated as an anode material for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  When tested as an anode for LIBs, the as-prepd. 3D porous SnO2@CC composite electrode delivered a discharge capacity of 1038 mA h g-1 over 200 cycles at a c.d. of 0.5 A g-1.  For SIBs, a discharge capacity of 498 mA h g-1 was delivered at 0.2 A g-1 over 100 cycles.  Even at 0.5 A g-1, the electrode exhibited a discharge capacity of 205 mA h g-1 over 100 cycles.  The excellent electrochem. properties of 3D porous SnO2/CC composite electrode for both lithium and sodium storage can be attributed to the good porous structure between the SnO2-NPs on the surface of CC and improved elec. cond. due to CC, which not only releases the strain during the Li+/Na+ insertion/extn. process but also can improve the ionic and electronic transportation.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref5" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2017.09.081"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duan, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Complexing Agent Engineered Strategy for Anchoring SnO<sub>2</sub> Nanoparticles on Sulfur/Nitrogen Co-Doped Graphene for Superior Lithium and Sodium Ion Storage</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Complexing agent engineered strategy for anchoring SnO2 nanoparticles on sulfur/nitrogen co-doped graphene for superior lithium and sodium ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Heng-guo; Jiang, Cheng; Yuan, Chenpei; Wu, Qiong; Li, Qiang; Duan, Qian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">332</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">237-244</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">An effective strategy is proposed and developed to prep. sulfur/nitrogen co-doped graphene/SnO2 composite (denoted SNGS).  The key point of this strategy is the choice of heteroatom-contg. org. compds., 5, 10, 15, 20-tetra-(4-sulfonatophenyl) porphyrin (TSPP), which can act as both the multi-heteroatom codoped source and the complexing agent.  After the calcination, the doped sulfur/nitrogen atoms could effectively pin SnO2 nanocrystals on graphene sheets due to the existence of the binding effect.  As a result, the unique feature as well as the synergetic effect between sulfur/nitrogen co-doped graphene and SnO2 nanocrystals endows the composite materials with good electrochem. performances as anode materials for lithium ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium ion batteries (SIBs), including high initial discharge capacity (1089 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 for LIBs and 673.8 mAh g-1 at 25 mA g-1 for SIBs) and reversible capacity (924.4 mAh g-1 after 150 cycles for LIBs and 264.9 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles for SIBs).  The strategy derived from heteroatom-contg. org. compds. might open new avenues for the design of high-performance doped graphene/metal oxide anode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref6" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.0c21447"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Si, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Iron Nitride@C Nanocubes inside Core-Shell Fibers to Realize High Air-Stability, Ultralong Life, and Superior Lithium/Sodium Storages</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Iron Nitride@C Nanocubes Inside Core-Shell Fibers to Realize High Air-Stability, Ultralong Life, and Superior Lithium/Sodium Storages</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Xiaolong; Deng, Chao; Wang, Hongmei; Si, Jiaqi; Zhang, Sen; Huang, Bing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Poor air stability and severe structure pulverization are crucial issues for metal nitrides in metal-ion batteries.  Herein, core-shell hybrid fibers (CSHN fiber) filled with metal nitride@C hollow nanocubes are introduced to be a new self-supporting anode for sodium-ion and lithium-ion batteries.  The hierarchical carbon network provides fast electronic pathways and gives high protection for iron nitrides.  Meanwhile, the self-supporting electrode avoids the complicated electrode fabrication process and decreases the opportunity to air exposure.  Moreover, its porous nature ensures high buffer to volumetric expansion and improves the cycling stability.  Therefore, it is a good platform to realize fast kinetics and high durability.  For the first time, Fe2N@N-doped carbon CSHN hybrid fibers are constructed.  Their influences on air stability and electrochem. behaviors are studied.  Impressively, they achieve high stabilities in both lithium-ion (92.8%, at 5 A g-1, 1000 cycles) and sodium-ion (95.6%, at 2 A g-1, 2000 cycles) batteries.  Therefore, this work introduces a new method to construct superior performance nitride anodes.  Moreover, it also provides a new insight on the fabrication of highly efficient structures for diverse functional materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref7" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2017.12.181"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Rational Design of SnO<sub>2</sub>@C@MnO<sub>2</sub> Hierarchical Hollow Hybrid Nanospheres for a Li-Ion Battery Anode with Enhanced Performances</span>. <i>Electrochim.         </div><div class="casAbstract">SnO2@C@MnO2 hierarchical hollow hybrid nanospheres were obtained by coating the MnO2 nanosheet-based hierarchical shell on SnO2@C hollow nanospheres via a redox method. SnO2@C@MnO2 nanomaterials exhibit a large initial discharge capacity (1378 mAhg-1), extraordinary cyclic stability (644.5 mAhg-1 after 200 cycles) and rate capability as Li-ion battery anodes.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Interface design is generally helpful to ameliorate the electrochem. properties of electrode materials but challenging as well.  Herein, in situ sulfur-mediated interface engineering is developed to effectively raise the kinetics properties of the SnS nanosheet anodes, which is realized by a synchronous redn. and carbon deposition/doping process.  The sulfur in the raw SnS2 directly induces the sulfur-doped amorphous carbon layer onto the in situ reduced SnS nanosheet.  In situ and ex situ electrochem. characterizations suggest that the sulfur-mediated interface layer can enhance the reversibility and kinetics properties, promote the ion/electron swift delivery, and maintain the configurational wholeness of the SnS nanosheet anodes.  Consequently, a relatively high Li-storage capacity of 922 mAh g-1 and Na-storage capacity of 349 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 even after 1000 and 300 long-term cycles are achieved, resp.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Biotemplating is an effective strategy to obtain morphol.-controllable materials with structural specificity, complexity, and corresponding unique functions.  Different from traditional biotemplating strategies replicating the morphol. and using biogenic elements of biomaterials (e.g., C, Si, N, Fe, P, S), the unique heavy-metal-ion biosorption behavior is taken advantage of microalgae to fabricate tin-decorated carbon (Sn@C) anode materials for lithium-ion batteries.  Microalgae Spirulina platensis is used as the biotemplate, the renewable carbon source, and the biosorbent.  After a facile one-step heat treatment, Sn@C with tin particles (20-30 nm) dispersing into the porous carbon matrix can be obtained. The Sn@C anode shows a discharge capacity of 520 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles, as well as excellent cycle stability and high coulombic efficiency (∼ 100%), exhibiting fascinating electrochem. performance.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ fabrication of nitrogen-doped carbon-coated SnO2/SnS heterostructures with enhanced performance for lithium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ye, Haijun; Li, Hongqin; Jiang, Fangqing; Yin, Jiao; Zhu, Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin-based compds. have incurred tremendous attention due to their higher specific capacities than their analogs for lithium storage. The electrochem. properties of the 3D SnS/C were examd. comprehensively as anode materials for lithium/sodium ion batteries (LIBs/SIBs). The rate performance is also excellent (550 mA h g-1 at 3 A g-1 in LIBs and 220.9 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1 in SIBs).  The outstanding electrochem. performance of the 3D SnS/C is ascribed to its 3D porous carbon interconnected structure and nanoconfined SnS nanoparticles distributing broadly in carbon matrix, which not only improve the cond., but also keep the structure integrity, and as a result of enhancing the cycling stability of the material.  In addn., this facile and novelty strategy can be potentially utilized for prepg. other 3D metal sulfides interconnected macroporous carbon composite for energy storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref12" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcis.2020.03.063"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.-N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Goktas, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Adelhelm, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, B.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrafine SnO2 nanoparticles anchored on N, P-doped porous carbon as anodes for high performance lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Ya-Nan; Goktas, Mustafa; Zhao, Li; Adelhelm, Philipp; Han, Bao-Hang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">An ultrafine tin dioxide/N, P-doped porous carbon (SnO2/NPPC) nanocomposite is prepd. through in-situ growth of tin dioxide (SnO2) nanoparticles in N, P-doped porous carbon (NPPC).  Owing to the in-situ growth method, the size of SnO2 nanoparticles in SnO2/NPPC is quite small and uniform (generally &lt; 5.0 nm).  NPPC provides a support and a conductive carbon skeleton for the SnO2 nanoparticles.  The small SnO2 nanoparticles are less likely to aggregate during the discharge-charge process due to the presence of Sn-O-C bonding and nanoconfinement effect of SnO2 nanoparticles in carbon matrix.  The N and P doping can provide abundant defects to facilitate the penetration of Li+ or Na+ into the interior of the electrode.  In addn., the presence of Sn-N bonding can further improve the electrochem. properties of the electrodes.  Thus, as an anode material for lithium-ion batteries, SnO2/NPPC possesses an enhanced rate performance, an excellent cycling stability, and a high initial Coulombic efficiency.  The structure of the ultrafine SnO2 nanoparticles is well maintained in cycled SnO2/NPPC.  Meanwhile, SnO2/NPPC also possesses good electrochem. performance as an anode for sodium-ion batteries.  The good electrochem. properties for SnO2/NPPC materials can be ascribed to the synergetic effect between small SnO2 nanoparticles and NPPC.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref13" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcis.2020.12.121"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Size-Controllable Synthesis of Zn<sub>2</sub>GeO<sub>4</sub> Hollow Rods Supported on Reduced Graphene Oxide as High-Capacity Anode for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Germanium-based ternary oxides have aroused wide attention as an anode for high-performance lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).  Nevertheless, they usually suffer a large vol. expansion and rapid capacity fading during lithiation/delithiation cycles.  To address this issue, herein, Zn2GeO4/RGO composites are synthesized with Zn2GeO4 hollow rods in-situ grown on reduced graphene oxide (RGO) sheets.  The Zn2GeO4 hollow rods can be facilely adjusted from nano- to micro-size.  The lithium storage performances of the composites strongly depend on the size of Zn2GeO4 hollow rods and the content of RGO.  The optimized Zn2GeO4/RGO composite exhibits a pseudocapacitance-dominated Li+ storage performance, with a large reversible capacity of 1005 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles at 0.5 A g-1, an excellent rate capability (515 mAh g-1 at a high rate of 5 A g-1) and a good long cycling stability of 500 cycles with a low capacity loss of 0.05% per cycle at 1 A g-1.  The outstanding electrochem. performance can be attributed to the unique compn. and microstructure of the material as well as the synergistic effect of the conductive RGO sheets and the hollow Zn2GeO4 nanostructure.  This work provides a promising anode for high-performance LIBs and a useful inspiration for further improving the Ge-based ternary oxide anodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref14" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcis.2020.11.115"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Template-Free Fabrication of 1D Core-Shell MoO<sub>2</sub>@MoS<sub>2</sub>/Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanorods for Enhanced Lithium/Sodium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Porous hollow ZnCo2S4 nanosheet arrays derived from metal-organic framework as efficient cathode for lithium oxygen batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Peng; Hui, Xiaobin; Wang, Huiyang; Gao, Xueping; Yin, Longwei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable non-aq. lithium oxygen batteries (LOBs) have attracted extensive attention as the most promising next-generation battery technologies due to their extremely high theor. energy d.  However, their practical applications are hampered by sluggish reaction kinetics and severe parasitic reactions, resulting from the insulating and insol. discharge product-Li2O2.  Herein, self-standing ZnCo2S4 nanosheet arrays derived from metal-org. framework (MOF) via low-temp. solvothermal sulfuration method, are fabricated as efficient cathode for LOBs.  The hollow structure of ZnCo2S4 nanosheet formed during sulfuration provides more catalytic sites and alleviates stress during repeated discharge/charge progress, while three-dimensional (3D) porous architecture inheriting from MOF shortens the transportation pathway of Li+ and O2 in electrolyte.         </div><div class="casAbstract">SnS2 has been widely studied as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) based on the high theor. capacity and layered structure.  Unfortunately, rapid capacity decay assocd. with vol. variation during cycling limits practical application. When applied as the anode for SIBs, the sample delivers a distinguished charge specific capacity of 1141.8 mAh g-1 and there is no significant capacity decay (0.1 A g-1 for 50 cycles).  When the rate is increased to 0.5 A g-1, it presents 845.7 mAh g-1 after cycling 100 times.  Furthermore, the composite also exhibits an ultrafast sodium storage capability where 392.9 mAh g-1 can be obtained at 10 A g-1 and the charging time is less than 3 min.  The outstanding electrochem. properties can be ascribed to the enhancement of cond. for the addn. of S-doped graphene and the existence of p-n junctions in the SnS2/Co3S4 heterostructure.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In an attempt to exploit ternary metal sulfides as high energy and high power anode material for lithium and sodium ion batteries, inhouse prepd. CuCo2S4 (CCS) nanoparticles, obtained through template free one pot solvothermal synthesis has been deployed.  Herein, particle size of CCS obtained below 50 nm helps to address two main challenges such as capacity fading and inferior rate capability behavior.  Further, we demonstrate the composite of CCS consisting of multi-walled carbon nanotube (MWCNT) in the form of CCS/MWCNT as potential anode for LIBs and SIBs. Similarly, CCS/MWCNT anode exhibits 181 mA h g-1 and 236 mA h g-1 at 5 and 1 A g-1 resp. upto 500 cycles in SIBs with 90 and 95% capacity retention, which is noteworthy.  CCS/MWCNT anode tolerates up to 20 A g-1 c.d. and delivers a capacity of 87 mA h g-1, thus qualifying itself as the versatile anode for application in LIBs and SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref21" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA01701D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Achieving Ultralong Life Sodium Storage in Amorphous Cobalt–Tin Binary Sulfide Nanoboxes Sheathed in N-Doped Carbon</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The interest in Na-ion batteries (NIBs) is growing exponentially since Na is more abundant and affordable than Li for large-scale energy storage applications.  However, the lack of truly durable and high-capacity electrode materials still remains a key bottle-neck issue for the development of practical NIBs.  In this work, we report the rational design of an ultra-long life anode material for NIBs by integrating the structural merits of hollow nanostructures, carbon nanocoating and amorphous structures together into a binary metal sulfide system. However, the fast capacity fading and the low power d. still limit their practical implementation.  In order to overcome these challenges, one-dimensional yolk-shell nanorods have been successfully constructed using manganese oxide as an example through a facile two-step sol-gel coating method.  Dopamine and tetraethoxysilane are used as precursors to obtain uniform polymer coating and silica layer followed by converting into carbon shell and hollow space, resp.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Germanium manganese oxide nanorods encapsulated by graphene sheets with enhanced electrochemical properties for lithium/sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Suresh babu, G. N.; Mani, V.; Nishanthi, S. T.; Nikhil Chandran, M. K.; Kalaiselvi, N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">This work demonstrates the possibility of deploying GeMn2O4/Graphene as an alternative anode for next generation lithium and sodium ion batteries.  Germanium, capable of forming an alloy with lithium and sodium, has been exploited as an electroactive material with a select combination of metals and functional matrix along with conducting graphene.  In other words, with a view to combat the known disadvantages of anodes, namely unavoidable vol. changes upon cycling and sluggish transport kinetics, morphol. tuned rods of GeMn2O4 (GMO) with the optimized addn. of graphene to form GeMn2O4/G (GMO/G) composite has been prepd. and investigated as an anode material.  In the GeMn2O4/G (GMO/G) composite, graphene enhances the electronic cond. and addresses the vol. variation during cycling esp. when tested against lithium and sodium counterparts individually.  For example, in Li-ion battery, GeMn2O4/G (GMO/G) exhibits a capacity of 1360 mA h g-1 even after 100 cycles, when cycled at a c.d. of 50 mA g-1.  As a SIB anode, GMO/G composite exhibits an appreciable capacity of 252 mA h g-1 upto 100 cycles at a c.d. of 50 mA g-1.  The obsd. capacity is attributed to the involvement of alloying/dealloying and conversion reactions related to Ge and Mn with lithium and sodium ions independently.  This remarkable performance can be exploited further to benefit the futuristic high capacity and high rate demanding lithium and sodium-ion battery applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref30" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1016/j.scib.2020.05.006"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cong, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">One-Pot Synthesis of Hierarchical CoS<sub>1-<i>x</i></sub>/NC@MoS<sub>2</sub>/C Hollow Nanofibers Based on One-Dimensional Metal Coordination Polymers for Enhanced Lithium and Sodium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>Sci.         (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Multicomponent metal sulfides have been recognized as promising anode materials for lithium/sodium-ion storage given their enticing theor. capacities.  However, the simplification of synthetic processes and the construction of heterogeneous interfaces of multimetal sulfides remain great challenges.  Herein, a hierarchical 1T-MoS2/carbon nanosheet decorated Co1-xS/N-doped carbon (Co1-xS/NC@MoS2/C) hollow nanofiber was designed and constructed via a one-pot hydrothermal method using a cobalt-based coordination polymer nanofiber.  This nanofiber can transform in-situ into conductive N-doped carbon hollow fibers embedded with active Co1-xS nanoparticles, enabling the epitaxial growth of MoS2 nanosheets.  Consequently, the Co1-xS/NC@MoS2/C composites achieve exceptional lithium/sodium-ion storage performance.  Compared to MoS2/C microspheres and Co1-xS/NC hollow nanofibers alone, the Co1-xS/NC@MoS2/C hollow nanofibers deliver higher discharge capacities (1085.9 mAh g-1 for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and 748.5 mAh g-1 for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) at 100 mA g-1), better capacity retention (910 mAh g-1 for LIBs and 636.5 mAh g-1 for SIBs after 150 cycles at 100 mA g-1), and increased cycling stability (407.2 mAh g-1 after 1000 cycles for SIBs at 1000 mA g-1).  Furthermore, the kinetic anal. shows that the lithium/sodium-ion storage processes of the Co1-xS/NC@MoS2/C electrode are mainly controlled by pseudocapacitance behavior.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Few-layered MoS2 with expanded interplanar spacing strongly encapsulated inside compact carbon spheres by C-S interaction as ultra-stable sodium-ion batteries anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Kunzhou; Guo, Jinze; Shen, Kaier; Ling, Rui; Cai, Shu; Sun, Xiaohong; Zheng, Chunming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">858</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">157675</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite-like metal sulfides, MoS2, is regarded as potential electrode of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) because of its relatively large interplanar spacing (0.62 nm) and outstanding theor. capacity (670 mA h g-1).  However, original MoS2 electrode often suffered from shortened cycle life and poor rate capability owing to the serious vol. change during sodium insertion/extn. and inferior inherent cond.  Herein, MoS2/C compact spheres (MoS2/C CSs) with dense structure constituted by few-layered MoS2 and conductive carbon coating are successfully developed using a in-situ synthesis method.  As anode of SIBs, MoS2/C CSs achieve a high capacity of 425 mA h g-1 after 200 cycles at 0.1 A g-1 with initial coulombic efficiency up to 84.8%.  The reversible capacity is still maintained in 320 mA h g-1 after 400 cycles at 1 A g-1, which is three times of original MoS2 (110 mA h g-1).  Besides, MoS2/C CSs also have considerable rate performance, reserving impressive capacity (310 mA h g-1) at 5.0 A g-1.  The compact and conductive carbon coating effectively inhibits vol. expansion and improves elec. cond., meanwhile, the few-layered MoS2 nanoflakes with ampliative interplanar spacing (0.73 nm) simplify the Na+ diffusion pathway and promote rapid diffusion of Na+.  Furthermore, the C-S chem. bond tightly interlocks MoS2 and C, which guarantees the above mechanisms synergistically and continuously intensify the property of MoS2/C CSs anode.  The above results are verified by ex-situ impedance, phase and morphol. anal.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref33" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcis.2020.10.062"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhuang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sandwich-Structured Graphene Hollow Spheres Limited Mn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub>/SnO<sub>2</sub> Heterostructures as Anode Materials for High-Performance Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sandwich-structured graphene hollow spheres limited Mn2SnO4/SnO2 heterostructures as anode materials for high-performance lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhuang, Hua; Han, Mingrui; Ma, Wencheng; Ou, Yanghao; Jiang, Yong; Li, Wenrong; Liu, Xiaoyu; Zhao, Bing; Zhang, Jiujun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">586</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1-10</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCISA5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0021-9797</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sn-based metal oxides and composites have been widely investigated as candidate anodes for lithium-ion batteries.  However, continuous capacity fade caused by serious volumetric expansion and crystal pulverization is often noticed during lithiation and alloying processes.  In this study, we design a novel heterogeneous structural composite by constructing sandwich-structured graphene hollow spheres limited Mn2SnO4/SnO2 heterostructures (Mn2SnO4/SnO2@SG), of which infiltration of Mn source promotes the dissoln.-redeposition of SnO2 in hollow-spherical graphene (SnO2@SG) and their in-situ transformation into Mn2SnO4; and the uniform distributed Mn2SnO4 and SnO2 nanoparticles are adjacent each other to form heterostructure within the sandwiched graphene hollow spheres.  By comparing with the single metal oxide SnO2@SG material, the influence of the microstructure, chem. compn., element valence state and electrochem. properties of the heterostructured Mn2SnO4/SnO2@SG is investigated.  The results show that the construction of Mn2SnO4/SnO2 heterostructure dramatically improves electronic/ionic transport kinetics and increases lithium storage reversibility, therefore leading to distinctly superior rate capability (823.8 mAh g-1 at 5 C) and cycling capacity.  An ultra-high discharge capacity of 1180.4 mA h g-1 is maintained up to 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1.  The promising electrochem. performances can be attributed to the sandwiched-structure hollow graphene spherical skeleton and the formation of unique Mn2SnO4/SnO2 heterostructures.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref34" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2019.134757"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, J.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Renewable agaric-based hierarchically porous cocoon-like MnO/Carbon composites enable high-energy and high-rate Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Ji; Luo, Jin-Di; Zhang, Hai; Zhang, Ze; Wei, Junchao; Yang, Zhenyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hierarchical pore structures in the composite electrode materials can offer greater accessibility to active sites for the Li ions, shorter ion diffusion distances and quicker Li ion diffusion, which can enable the high-rate and high-energy Li-ion batteries (LIBs).  Hierarchically porous cocoon-like MnO/C composites (PCM) were prepd. using natural agaric as raw materials via a sustainable and facile method assocd. with the hydrothermal and annealing treatment.  The as-prepd. porous PCM composites show a high reversible capacity of 981 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 and remain an high discharge capacity of 640 mAh g-1 after 900 cycles at 1 A g-1.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile Preparation of Porous Mn2SnO4/Sn/C Composite Cubes as High Performance Anode Material for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Kuang; Cheang, Tuck-Yun; Wen, Tao; Xie, Xiao; Zhou, Xiao; Zhao, Zhi-Wei; Shen, Cong-Cong; Jiang, Nan; Xu, An-Wu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In recent years, Sn-based materials have been explored as potential anodes for high energy lithium-ion batteries.  However, their severe vol. expansion in lithiation procedure could lead to poor cycling property and inferior rate capability, which limit the applications of Sn-based materials in lithium-ion batteries.  In this study, we have designed and prepd. uniform Mn2SnO4/Sn/carbon composite cubic particles with a porous structure as anode material through facile hydrothermal method and subsequent annealing process. The remarkable performance can be attributed to the formation of unique conductive frameworks and the porous structure.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref36" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.9b22368"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fei, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xin, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Selegard, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Uvdal, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Integrated Design of Hierarchical CoSnO<sub>3</sub>@NC@MnO@NC Nanobox as Anode Material for Enhanced Lithium Storage Performance</span>. <i>ACS Appl.
